âš–ï¸ MASTERY BRIEF: POST-FILING CONVERSION STRATEGY IN MICHIGAN COURTS
ğŸ”· SCENARIO CONTEXT
A motion for injunction or a verified complaint has been filed and served, and the court has already granted part of the relief (e.g., preliminary or permanent injunction, declaratory relief). Now Plaintiff wants to convert that procedural momentum into:

A formal damages complaint

A monetary judgment request

A trial posture

A post-judgment modification or enforcement sequence

ğŸ§  LEGAL FRAMEWORK (MICHIGAN COURT RULES)
Rule	Authority	Conversion Use
MCR 2.118	Amended and Supplemental Pleadings	Governs amendment of complaints post-filing, including adding claims for damages after declaratory/injunctive relief is granted.
MCR 2.119(F)	Motions for Rehearing or Modification	Used if an order needs to be expanded or modified to include monetary relief
MCR 2.611â€“2.612	Relief from Judgment	Applicable if you're seeking to alter a judgment after the fact (e.g., adding vacatur, restitution, etc.)
MCR 2.116(C)(10)	Motion for Summary Disposition â€“ No Genuine Issue of Material Fact	Once liability is declared (e.g., through an injunction), file for damages judgment directly if material facts are resolved
MCR 2.401(C)	Case Management Orders	Modify or request new scheduling deadlines for added phases (e.g., damages hearing after injunction)
MCR 2.605	Declaratory Judgment	Allows you to ask for further relief following declaratory findings already issued (e.g., â€œthe court having declared the act unlawful, now award monetary reliefâ€)
ğŸ› ï¸ PRACTICAL STRATEGY FOR CONVERSION
ğŸ” A. From Injunction â†’ Damages
Attach the already-granted injunction/declaratory order as Exhibit A.

Draft a Motion for Entry of Judgment or Amended Complaint for Damages under MCR 2.118(A)(2).

Argue that the court has already found liability (e.g., unlawful eviction), so what remains is valuation of harm and damages.

Request either:

(a) Bench trial on damages only, or

(b) Summary disposition under MCR 2.116(C)(10) if damages are fully proven.

âš–ï¸ Example:
"The Courtâ€™s Order of August 12, 2025 established the unlawfulness of Defendantsâ€™ actions as a matter of law. Pursuant to MCR 2.116(C)(10), Plaintiff now seeks summary adjudication on damages."

ğŸ§© B. From Motion â†’ Complaint (Recast as Formal Pleading)
Motions (e.g., for injunction, declaratory judgment) that included factual allegations and exhibits can be restructured into a formal complaint.

File either:

A Verified Amended Complaint

Or a Motion to Treat Existing Motion as Verified Complaint and seek relief under MCR 2.605 + MCR 2.118(B)

Cite judicial economy and already-served parties to avoid duplication or new service.

ğŸ” Use Case:
A motion for preliminary injunction (with affidavit, exhibits) becomes the foundation of a permanent complaint, especially when court has ruled on facts.

ğŸ”§ C. Conversion Checklist
Step	Description
âœ… 1. Anchor to Existing Order	Reference final court findings (e.g., unlawful eviction, misrepresentation).
âœ… 2. File Motion for Leave to Amend (if complaint)	Use MCR 2.118(A)(2) (courtâ€™s permission) or 2.118(B) (implied consent).
âœ… 3. Serve Amended Complaint (if adding new parties)	Not necessary for existing defendants unless adding new claims.
âœ… 4. Prepare for Damages Hearing or Bench Trial	Use case scheduling tools under MCR 2.401 and MCR 2.501.
âœ… 5. Attach Valuation Matrix and Exhibits	Lock in statutory multipliers, proof of loss, and trauma testimony.
ğŸ“ CITATIONS AND PRECEDENT
Taylor v. Blue Cross Blue Shield of Mich, 205 Mich App 644 (1994):

Courts have broad discretion under MCR 2.118 to permit post-filing amendments to conform with proof or court findings.

Yudashkin v. Linzmeyer, 247 Mich App 642 (2001):

Declaratory relief may be followed by compensatory relief if rights and liability have been resolved.

MCR 2.605(D):

â€œFurther necessary or proper relief based on a declaratory judgment may be granted after reasonable notice and hearing.â€

ğŸ” PAGE 2 â€“ LEASE ANALYSIS: â€œNO LIABILITY, ABSOLUTE CONTROLâ€ SCAN
Document: Andrew Pigors Lease_20250107182535.pdf
Page: 2

CONTENT SUMMARY & LEGAL TARGETS
Key Clauses and Language (Scrutiny for Defendant Escape Theory):
Extensive Disclaimer/Indemnity Language:
Landlord attempts to disclaim responsibility for damages, injury, personal property loss, and â€œevents beyond its control.â€

Legal Counter: MCL 554.139 and MCL 600.2918 prohibit waiver of habitability, safety, or statutory eviction protections. Such disclaimers are void as against public policy in residential leases.

NO lease may exculpate a landlord from liability for their own statutory violations or intentional torts.

Limitation of Remedies/â€œOnly Damages, Not Possessionâ€ Clause:

Attempts to restrict tenant relief to monetary damages, denying injunctive relief, equitable remedies, or challenge to landlord conduct.

Legal Counter: MCR 3.310 (Injunctive relief) is governed by court, not by contract; parties cannot contractually eliminate access to equitable relief.

Absolute Right of Entry/Inspection Language:

Purports to allow landlord â€œanytimeâ€ entry for inspection, emergency, or â€œcommunity rule enforcement.â€

Legal Counter: MCL 600.2918(2)(c) criminalizes entry into a mobile home owned by the tenant without court orderâ€”even if the lease claims otherwise. Michigan courts have repeatedly held that lease â€œinspectionâ€ rights do not override statutory rights of titled owners.

ADMISSIBILITY & STRATEGIC WEAKNESSES (TO DESTROY LEASE ARGUMENT):
ğŸ”¨ Flaw	Legal Attack
Attempted Waiver of Statutory Protections	Void under MCL 554.139(2) and Michigan public policy.
Exculpatory Language for Landlord Negligence/Intentional Acts	Michigan case law: Lease cannot protect landlord from intentional tort or statutory violation. See Kitchen v. Kitchen, 465 Mich 654
Blanket Entry Rights	If used to justify July 14, 2025 entry/destruction, statutorily criminal; lease cannot legalize what statute forbids.
No Notary or Independent Witness	Weakens authenticity/enforceability of â€œconsentâ€ for entry or indemnification.
Ambiguity in â€œCommunity Rulesâ€ Enforcement	Vague terms are construed against drafter (contra proferentem rule).
